I've uploaded a python code repository in the directory /testbed/repo. Consider the following PR description:

<pr_description>
Dynamic Filter Pushdown is being applied to the wrong table
### Describe the bug

In the following example, the Dynamic Filter Pushdown is built from `t2 (k, v)` and correctly pushed to `t1 (k)`, to reduce the number of scanned rows from `t1`:

```sql
select *
from t1 -- 1M rows, will become the right side
join t2 on t1.k = t2.k
where t2.v = 1000000; -- 1 row, will become the left side

HashJoinExec join_type=Inner build_time=78.306µs, join_time=22.402µs
    DataSourceExec t2.parquet
        predicate=v@1 = 1000000
        output_rows=1
    DataSourceExec t1.parquet
        predicate=DynamicFilterPhysicalExpr [ k@0 >= 1000000 AND k@0 <= 1000000 ] -- dynamic filter added here
        output_rows=1 -- only returns 1 row
```

Now if the `t2` side is greater than `t1`, then the order of the join switches, as the smaller relation becomes the build side. However, the Dynamic Filter Pushdown is still applied to the right relation (now `t2`) instead of `t1`:

```sql
select *
from t1 -- 1M rows, will become the left side
join t2 on t1.k = t2.k
where t2.v >= 1000000; -- 9M rows, will become the right side

HashJoinExec join_type=Inner build_time=54.3462ms, join_time=2.403µs -- join is more expensive
    DataSourceExec t1.parquet
        output_rows=1000000
    DataSourceExec t2.parquet
        predicate=v@1 >= 1000000 AND DynamicFilterPhysicalExpr [ k@0 >= 3 AND k@0 <= 999998 ] -- dynamic filter added here
        output_rows=0 -- should be 1, possibly due to issue https://github.com/apache/datafusion/issues/17188
```

### To Reproduce

```sql
copy (select i as k from generate_series(1, 1000000) t(i)) to 't1.parquet';
copy (select i as k, i as v from generate_series(1, 10000000) t(i)) to 't2.parquet';
create external table t1 stored as parquet location 't1.parquet';
create external table t2 stored as parquet location 't2.parquet';

-- works
explain analyze select *
from t1
join t2 on t1.k = t2.k
where t2.v = 1000000;

-- pushed to the wrong relation
explain analyze select *
from t1
join t2 on t1.k = t2.k
where t2.v >= 1000000;
```

### Expected behavior

Dynamic Filter applied to the correct table.

### Additional context

_No response_

</pr_description>

    18	//! Filter Pushdown Optimization Process
    19	//!
    20	//! The filter pushdown mechanism involves four key steps:
    21	//! 1. **Optimizer Asks Parent for a Filter Pushdown Plan**: The optimizer calls [`ExecutionPlan::gather_filters_for_pushdown`]
    22	//!    on the parent node, passing in parent predicates and phase. The parent node creates a [`FilterDescription`]
    23	//!    by inspecting its logic and children's schemas, determining which filters can be pushed to each child.
    24	//! 2. **Optimizer Executes Pushdown**: The optimizer recursively calls `push_down_filters` in this module on each child,
    25	//!    passing the appropriate filters (`Vec<Arc<dyn PhysicalExpr>>`) for that child.
    26	//! 3. **Optimizer Gathers Results**: The optimizer collects [`FilterPushdownPropagation`] results from children,
    27	//!    containing information about which filters were successfully pushed down vs. unsupported.
    28	//! 4. **Parent Responds**: The optimizer calls [`ExecutionPlan::handle_child_pushdown_result`] on the parent,
    29	//!    passing a [`ChildPushdownResult`] containing the aggregated pushdown outcomes. The parent decides
    30	//!    how to handle filters that couldn't be pushed down (e.g., keep them as FilterExec nodes).
    31	//!
    32	//! [`FilterDescription`]: datafusion_physical_plan::filter_pushdown::FilterDescription
    33	
    34	use std::sync::Arc;
    35	
    36	use crate::PhysicalOptimizerRule;
    37	
    38	use datafusion_common::tree_node::{TreeNode, TreeNodeRecursion};
    39	use datafusion_common::{config::ConfigOptions, Result};
    40	use datafusion_expr_common::signature::Volatility;
    41	use datafusion_physical_expr::PhysicalExpr;
    42	use datafusion_physical_plan::filter_pushdown::{
    43	    ChildFilterPushdownResult, ChildPushdownResult, FilterPushdownPhase,
    44	    FilterPushdownPropagation, PushedDown,
    45	};
    46	use datafusion_physical_plan::{with_new_children_if_necessary, ExecutionPlan};
    47	
    48	use itertools::{izip, Itertools};
    49	
    50	/// Attempts to recursively push given filters from the top of the tree into leafs.
    51	///
    52	/// # Default Implementation
    53	///
    54	/// The default implementation in [`ExecutionPlan::gather_filters_for_pushdown`]
    55	/// and [`ExecutionPlan::handle_child_pushdown_result`] assumes that:
    56	///
    57	/// * Parent filters can't be passed onto children (determined by [`ExecutionPlan::gather_filters_for_pushdown`])
    58	/// * This node has no filters to contribute (determined by [`ExecutionPlan::gather_filters_for_pushdown`]).
    59	/// * Any filters that could not be pushed down to the children are marked as unsupported (determined by [`ExecutionPlan::handle_child_pushdown_result`]).
    60	///
    61	/// # Example: Push filter into a `DataSourceExec`
    62	///
    63	/// For example, consider the following plan:
    64	///
    65	/// ```text
    66	/// ┌──────────────────────┐
    67	/// │ CoalesceBatchesExec  │
    68	/// └──────────────────────┘
    69	///             │
    70	///             ▼
    71	/// ┌──────────────────────┐
    72	/// │      FilterExec      │
    73	/// │  filters = [ id=1]   │
    74	/// └──────────────────────┘
    75	///             │
    76	///             ▼
    77	/// ┌──────────────────────┐
    78	/// │    DataSourceExec    │
    79	/// │    projection = *    │
    80	/// └──────────────────────┘
    81	/// ```
    82	///
    83	/// Our goal is to move the `id = 1` filter from the [`FilterExec`] node to the `DataSourceExec` node.
    84	///
    85	/// If this filter is selective pushing it into the scan can avoid massive
    86	/// amounts of data being read from the source (the projection is `*` so all
    87	/// matching columns are read).
    88	///
    89	/// The new plan looks like:
    90	///
    91	/// ```text
    92	/// ┌──────────────────────┐
    93	/// │ CoalesceBatchesExec  │
    94	/// └──────────────────────┘
    95	///           │
    96	///           ▼
    97	/// ┌──────────────────────┐
    98	/// │    DataSourceExec    │
    99	/// │    projection = *    │
   100	/// │   filters = [ id=1]  │
   101	/// └──────────────────────┘
   102	/// ```
   103	///
   104	/// # Example: Push filters with `ProjectionExec`
   105	///
   106	/// Let's consider a more complex example involving a [`ProjectionExec`]
   107	/// node in between the [`FilterExec`] and `DataSourceExec` nodes that
   108	/// creates a new column that the filter depends on.
   109	///
   110	/// ```text
   111	/// ┌──────────────────────┐
   112	/// │ CoalesceBatchesExec  │
   113	/// └──────────────────────┘
   114	///             │
   115	///             ▼
   116	/// ┌──────────────────────┐
   117	/// │      FilterExec      │
   118	/// │    filters =         │
   119	/// │     [cost>50,id=1]   │
   120	/// └──────────────────────┘
   121	///             │
   122	///             ▼
   123	/// ┌──────────────────────┐
   124	/// │    ProjectionExec    │
   125	/// │ cost = price * 1.2   │
   126	/// └──────────────────────┘
   127	///             │
   128	///             ▼
   129	/// ┌──────────────────────┐
   130	/// │    DataSourceExec    │
   131	/// │    projection = *    │
   132	/// └──────────────────────┘
   133	/// ```
   134	///
   135	/// We want to push down the filters `[id=1]` to the `DataSourceExec` node,
   136	/// but can't push down `cost>50` because it requires the [`ProjectionExec`]
   137	/// node to be executed first. A simple thing to do would be to split up the
   138	/// filter into two separate filters and push down the first one:
   139	///
   140	/// ```text
   141	/// ┌──────────────────────┐
   142	/// │ CoalesceBatchesExec  │
   143	/// └──────────────────────┘
   144	///             │
   145	///             ▼
   146	/// ┌──────────────────────┐
   147	/// │      FilterExec      │
   148	/// │    filters =         │
   149	/// │     [cost>50]        │
   150	/// └──────────────────────┘
   151	///             │
   152	///             ▼
   153	/// ┌──────────────────────┐
   154	/// │    ProjectionExec    │
   155	/// │ cost = price * 1.2   │
   156	/// └──────────────────────┘
   157	///             │
   158	///             ▼
   159	/// ┌──────────────────────┐
   160	/// │    DataSourceExec    │
   161	/// │    projection = *    │
   162	/// │   filters = [ id=1]  │
   163	/// └──────────────────────┘
   164	/// ```
   165	///
   166	/// We can actually however do better by pushing down `price * 1.2 > 50`
   167	/// instead of `cost > 50`:
   168	///
   169	/// ```text
   170	/// ┌──────────────────────┐
   171	/// │ CoalesceBatchesExec  │
   172	/// └──────────────────────┘
   173	///            │
   174	///            ▼
   175	/// ┌──────────────────────┐
   176	/// │    ProjectionExec    │
   177	/// │ cost = price * 1.2   │
   178	/// └──────────────────────┘
   179	///            │
   180	///            ▼
   181	/// ┌──────────────────────┐
   182	/// │    DataSourceExec    │
   183	/// │    projection = *    │
   184	/// │   filters = [id=1,   │
   185	/// │   price * 1.2 > 50]  │
   186	/// └──────────────────────┘
   187	/// ```
   188	///
   189	/// # Example: Push filters within a subtree
   190	///
   191	/// There are also cases where we may be able to push down filters within a
   192	/// subtree but not the entire tree. A good example of this is aggregation
   193	/// nodes:
   194	///
   195	/// ```text
   196	/// ┌──────────────────────┐
   197	/// │ ProjectionExec       │
   198	/// │ projection = *       │
   199	/// └──────────────────────┘
   200	///           │
   201	///           ▼
   202	/// ┌──────────────────────┐
   203	/// │ FilterExec           │
   204	/// │ filters = [sum > 10] │
   205	/// └──────────────────────┘
   206	///           │
   207	///           ▼
   208	/// ┌───────────────────────┐
   209	/// │     AggregateExec     │
   210	/// │    group by = [id]    │
   211	/// │    aggregate =        │
   212	/// │      [sum(price)]     │
   213	/// └───────────────────────┘
   214	///           │
   215	///           ▼
   216	/// ┌──────────────────────┐
   217	/// │ FilterExec           │
   218	/// │ filters = [id=1]     │
   219	/// └──────────────────────┘
   220	///          │
   221	///          ▼
   222	/// ┌──────────────────────┐
   223	/// │ DataSourceExec       │
   224	/// │ projection = *       │
   225	/// └──────────────────────┘
   226	/// ```
   227	///
   228	/// The transformation here is to push down the `id=1` filter to the
   229	/// `DataSourceExec` node:
   230	///
   231	/// ```text
   232	/// ┌──────────────────────┐
   233	/// │ ProjectionExec       │
   234	/// │ projection = *       │
   235	/// └──────────────────────┘
   236	///           │
   237	///           ▼
   238	/// ┌──────────────────────┐
   239	/// │ FilterExec           │
   240	/// │ filters = [sum > 10] │
   241	/// └──────────────────────┘
   242	///           │
   243	///           ▼
   244	/// ┌───────────────────────┐
   245	/// │     AggregateExec     │
   246	/// │    group by = [id]    │
   247	/// │    aggregate =        │
   248	/// │      [sum(price)]     │
   249	/// └───────────────────────┘
   250	///           │
   251	///           ▼
   252	/// ┌──────────────────────┐
   253	/// │ DataSourceExec       │
   254	/// │ projection = *       │
   255	/// │ filters = [id=1]     │
   256	/// └──────────────────────┘
   257	/// ```
   258	///
   259	/// The point here is that:
   260	/// 1. We cannot push down `sum > 10` through the [`AggregateExec`] node into the `DataSourceExec` node.
   261	///    Any filters above the [`AggregateExec`] node are not pushed down.
   262	///    This is determined by calling [`ExecutionPlan::gather_filters_for_pushdown`] on the [`AggregateExec`] node.
   263	/// 2. We need to keep recursing into the tree so that we can discover the other [`FilterExec`] node and push
   264	///    down the `id=1` filter.
   265	///
   266	/// # Example: Push filters through Joins
   267	///
   268	/// It is also possible to push down filters through joins and filters that
   269	/// originate from joins. For example, a hash join where we build a hash
   270	/// table of the left side and probe the right side (ignoring why we would
   271	/// choose this order, typically it depends on the size of each table,
   272	/// etc.).
   273	///
   274	/// ```text
   275	///              ┌─────────────────────┐
   276	///              │     FilterExec      │
   277	///              │ filters =           │
   278	///              │  [d.size > 100]     │
   279	///              └─────────────────────┘
   280	///                         │
   281	///                         │
   282	///              ┌──────────▼──────────┐
   283	///              │                     │
   284	///              │    HashJoinExec     │
   285	///              │ [u.dept@hash(d.id)] │
   286	///              │                     │
   287	///              └─────────────────────┘
   288	///                         │
   289	///            ┌────────────┴────────────┐
   290	/// ┌──────────▼──────────┐   ┌──────────▼──────────┐
   291	/// │   DataSourceExec    │   │   DataSourceExec    │
   292	/// │  alias [users as u] │   │  alias [dept as d]  │
   293	/// │                     │   │                     │
   294	/// └─────────────────────┘   └─────────────────────┘
   295	/// ```
   296	///
   297	/// There are two pushdowns we can do here:
   298	/// 1. Push down the `d.size > 100` filter through the `HashJoinExec` node to the `DataSourceExec`
   299	///    node for the `departments` table.
   300	/// 2. Push down the hash table state from the `HashJoinExec` node to the `DataSourceExec` node to avoid reading
   301	///    rows from the `users` table that will be eliminated by the join.
   302	///    This can be done via a bloom filter or similar and is not (yet) supported
   303	///    in DataFusion. See <https://github.com/apache/datafusion/issues/7955>.
   304	///
   305	/// ```text
   306	///              ┌─────────────────────┐
   307	///              │                     │
   308	///              │    HashJoinExec     │
   309	///              │ [u.dept@hash(d.id)] │
   310	///              │                     │
   311	///              └─────────────────────┘
   312	///                         │
   313	///            ┌────────────┴────────────┐
   314	/// ┌──────────▼──────────┐   ┌──────────▼──────────┐
   315	/// │   DataSourceExec    │   │   DataSourceExec    │
   316	/// │  alias [users as u] │   │  alias [dept as d]  │
   317	/// │ filters =           │   │  filters =          │
   318	/// │   [depg@hash(d.id)] │   │    [ d.size > 100]  │
   319	/// └─────────────────────┘   └─────────────────────┘
   320	/// ```
   321	///
   322	/// You may notice in this case that the filter is *dynamic*: the hash table
   323	/// is built _after_ the `departments` table is read and at runtime. We
   324	/// don't have a concrete `InList` filter or similar to push down at
   325	/// optimization time. These sorts of dynamic filters are handled by
   326	/// building a specialized [`PhysicalExpr`] that can be evaluated at runtime
   327	/// and internally maintains a reference to the hash table or other state.
   328	///
   329	/// To make working with these sorts of dynamic filters more tractable we have the method [`PhysicalExpr::snapshot`]
   330	/// which attempts to simplify a dynamic filter into a "basic" non-dynamic filter.
   331	/// For a join this could mean converting it to an `InList` filter or a min/max filter for example.
   332	/// See `datafusion/physical-plan/src/dynamic_filters.rs` for more details.
   333	///
   334	/// # Example: Push TopK filters into Scans
   335	///
   336	/// Another form of dynamic filter is pushing down the state of a `TopK`
   337	/// operator for queries like `SELECT * FROM t ORDER BY id LIMIT 10`:
   338	///
   339	/// ```text
   340	/// ┌──────────────────────┐
   341	/// │       TopK           │
   342	/// │     limit = 10       │
   343	/// │   order by = [id]    │
   344	/// └──────────────────────┘
   345	///            │
   346	///            ▼
   347	/// ┌──────────────────────┐
   348	/// │    DataSourceExec    │
   349	/// │    projection = *    │
   350	/// └──────────────────────┘
   351	/// ```
   352	///
   353	/// We can avoid large amounts of data processing by transforming this into:
   354	///
   355	/// ```text
   356	/// ┌──────────────────────┐
   357	/// │       TopK           │
   358	/// │     limit = 10       │
   359	/// │   order by = [id]    │
   360	/// └──────────────────────┘
   361	///            │
   362	///            ▼
   363	/// ┌──────────────────────┐
   364	/// │    DataSourceExec    │
   365	/// │    projection = *    │
   366	/// │ filters =            │
   367	/// │    [id < @ TopKHeap] │
   368	/// └──────────────────────┘
   369	/// ```
   370	///
   371	/// Now as we fill our `TopK` heap we can push down the state of the heap to
   372	/// the `DataSourceExec` node to avoid reading files / row groups / pages /
   373	/// rows that could not possibly be in the top 10.
   374	///
   375	/// This is not yet implemented in DataFusion. See
   376	/// <https://github.com/apache/datafusion/issues/15037>
   377	///
   378	/// [`PhysicalExpr`]: datafusion_physical_plan::PhysicalExpr
   379	/// [`PhysicalExpr::snapshot`]: datafusion_physical_plan::PhysicalExpr::snapshot
   380	/// [`FilterExec`]: datafusion_physical_plan::filter::FilterExec
   381	/// [`ProjectionExec`]: datafusion_physical_plan::projection::ProjectionExec
   382	/// [`AggregateExec`]: datafusion_physical_plan::aggregates::AggregateExec
   383	#[derive(Debug)]
   384	pub struct FilterPushdown {
   385	    phase: FilterPushdownPhase,
   386	    name: String,
   387	}
   388	
   389	impl FilterPushdown {
   390	    fn new_with_phase(phase: FilterPushdownPhase) -> Self {
   391	        let name = match phase {
   392	            FilterPushdownPhase::Pre => "FilterPushdown",
   393	            FilterPushdownPhase::Post => "FilterPushdown(Post)",
   394	        }
   395	        .to_string();
   396	        Self { phase, name }
   397	    }
   398	
   399	    /// Create a new [`FilterPushdown`] optimizer rule that runs in the pre-optimization phase.
   400	    /// See [`FilterPushdownPhase`] for more details.
   401	    pub fn new() -> Self {
   402	        Self::new_with_phase(FilterPushdownPhase::Pre)
   403	    }
   404	
   405	    /// Create a new [`FilterPushdown`] optimizer rule that runs in the post-optimization phase.
   406	    /// See [`FilterPushdownPhase`] for more details.
   407	    pub fn new_post_optimization() -> Self {
   408	        Self::new_with_phase(FilterPushdownPhase::Post)
   409	    }
   410	}
   411	
   412	impl Default for FilterPushdown {
   413	    fn default() -> Self {
   414	        Self::new()
   415	    }
   416	}
   417	
   418	impl PhysicalOptimizerRule for FilterPushdown {
   419	    fn optimize(
   420	        &self,
   421	        plan: Arc<dyn ExecutionPlan>,
   422	        config: &ConfigOptions,
   423	    ) -> Result<Arc<dyn ExecutionPlan>> {
   424	        Ok(
   425	            push_down_filters(Arc::clone(&plan), vec![], config, self.phase)?
   426	                .updated_node
   427	                .unwrap_or(plan),
   428	        )
   429	    }
   430	
   431	    fn name(&self) -> &str {
   432	        &self.name
   433	    }
   434	
   435	    fn schema_check(&self) -> bool {
   436	        true // Filter pushdown does not change the schema of the plan
   437	    }
   438	}
   439

    34	/// A dynamic [`PhysicalExpr`] that can be updated by anyone with a reference to it.
    35	///
    36	/// Any `ExecutionPlan` that uses this expression and holds a reference to it internally should probably also
    37	/// implement `ExecutionPlan::reset_state` to remain compatible with recursive queries and other situations where
    38	/// the same `ExecutionPlan` is reused with different data.
    39	#[derive(Debug)]
    40	pub struct DynamicFilterPhysicalExpr {
    41	    /// The original children of this PhysicalExpr, if any.
    42	    /// This is necessary because the dynamic filter may be initialized with a placeholder (e.g. `lit(true)`)
    43	    /// and later remapped to the actual expressions that are being filtered.
    44	    /// But we need to know the children (e.g. columns referenced in the expression) ahead of time to evaluate the expression correctly.
    45	    children: Vec<Arc<dyn PhysicalExpr>>,
    46	    /// If any of the children were remapped / modified (e.g. to adjust for projections) we need to keep track of the new children
    47	    /// so that when we update `current()` in subsequent iterations we can re-apply the replacements.
    48	    remapped_children: Option<Vec<Arc<dyn PhysicalExpr>>>,
    49	    /// The source of dynamic filters.
    50	    inner: Arc<RwLock<Inner>>,
    51	    /// For testing purposes track the data type and nullability to make sure they don't change.
    52	    /// If they do, there's a bug in the implementation.
    53	    /// But this can have overhead in production, so it's only included in our tests.
    54	    data_type: Arc<RwLock<Option<DataType>>>,
    55	    nullable: Arc<RwLock<Option<bool>>>,
    56	}
    57	
    58	#[derive(Debug)]
    59	struct Inner {
    60	    /// A counter that gets incremented every time the expression is updated so that we can track changes cheaply.
    61	    /// This is used for [`PhysicalExpr::snapshot_generation`] to have a cheap check for changes.
    62	    generation: u64,
    63	    expr: Arc<dyn PhysicalExpr>,
    64	}
    65	
    66	impl Inner {
    67	    fn new(expr: Arc<dyn PhysicalExpr>) -> Self {
    68	        Self {
    69	            // Start with generation 1 which gives us a different result for [`PhysicalExpr::generation`] than the default 0.
    70	            // This is not currently used anywhere but it seems useful to have this simple distinction.
    71	            generation: 1,
    72	            expr,
    73	        }
    74	    }
    75	}
    76	
    77	impl Hash for DynamicFilterPhysicalExpr {
    78	    fn hash<H: std::hash::Hasher>(&self, state: &mut H) {
    79	        let inner = self.current().expect("Failed to get current expression");
    80	        inner.dyn_hash(state);
    81	        self.children.dyn_hash(state);
    82	        self.remapped_children.dyn_hash(state);
    83	    }
    84	}
    85	
    86	impl PartialEq for DynamicFilterPhysicalExpr {
    87	    fn eq(&self, other: &Self) -> bool {
    88	        let inner = self.current().expect("Failed to get current expression");
    89	        let our_children = self.remapped_children.as_ref().unwrap_or(&self.children);
    90	        let other_children = other.remapped_children.as_ref().unwrap_or(&other.children);
    91	        let other = other.current().expect("Failed to get current expression");
    92	        inner.dyn_eq(other.as_any()) && our_children == other_children
    93	    }
    94	}
    95	
    96	impl Eq for DynamicFilterPhysicalExpr {}
    97	
    98	impl Display for DynamicFilterPhysicalExpr {
    99	    fn fmt(&self, f: &mut std::fmt::Formatter<'_>) -> std::fmt::Result {
   100	        let inner = self.current().expect("Failed to get current expression");
   101	        write!(f, "DynamicFilterPhysicalExpr [ {inner} ]")
   102	    }
   103	}
   104	
   105	impl DynamicFilterPhysicalExpr {
   106	    /// Create a new [`DynamicFilterPhysicalExpr`]
   107	    /// from an initial expression and a list of children.
   108	    /// The list of children is provided separately because
   109	    /// the initial expression may not have the same children.
   110	    /// For example, if the initial expression is just `true`
   111	    /// it will not reference any columns, but we may know that
   112	    /// we are going to replace this expression with a real one
   113	    /// that does reference certain columns.
   114	    /// In this case you **must** pass in the columns that will be
   115	    /// used in the final expression as children to this function
   116	    /// since DataFusion is generally not compatible with dynamic
   117	    /// *children* in expressions.
   118	    ///
   119	    /// To determine the children you can:
   120	    ///
   121	    /// - Use [`collect_columns`] to collect the columns from the expression.
   122	    /// - Use existing information, such as the sort columns in a `SortExec`.
   123	    ///
   124	    /// Generally the important bit is that the *leaf children that reference columns
   125	    /// do not change* since those will be used to determine what columns need to read or projected
   126	    /// when evaluating the expression.
   127	    ///
   128	    /// Any `ExecutionPlan` that uses this expression and holds a reference to it internally should probably also
   129	    /// implement `ExecutionPlan::reset_state` to remain compatible with recursive queries and other situations where
   130	    /// the same `ExecutionPlan` is reused with different data.
   131	    ///
   132	    /// [`collect_columns`]: crate::utils::collect_columns
   133	    pub fn new(
   134	        children: Vec<Arc<dyn PhysicalExpr>>,
   135	        inner: Arc<dyn PhysicalExpr>,
   136	    ) -> Self {
   137	        Self {
   138	            children,
   139	            remapped_children: None, // Initially no remapped children
   140	            inner: Arc::new(RwLock::new(Inner::new(inner))),
   141	            data_type: Arc::new(RwLock::new(None)),
   142	            nullable: Arc::new(RwLock::new(None)),
   143	        }
   144	    }
   145	
   146	    fn remap_children(
   147	        children: &[Arc<dyn PhysicalExpr>],
   148	        remapped_children: Option<&Vec<Arc<dyn PhysicalExpr>>>,
   149	        expr: Arc<dyn PhysicalExpr>,
   150	    ) -> Result<Arc<dyn PhysicalExpr>> {
   151	        if let Some(remapped_children) = remapped_children {
   152	            // Remap the children to the new children
   153	            // of the expression.
   154	            expr.transform_up(|child| {
   155	                // Check if this is any of our original children
   156	                if let Some(pos) =
   157	                    children.iter().position(|c| c.as_ref() == child.as_ref())
   158	                {
   159	                    // If so, remap it to the current children
   160	                    // of the expression.
   161	                    let new_child = Arc::clone(&remapped_children[pos]);
   162	                    Ok(Transformed::yes(new_child))
   163	                } else {
   164	                    // Otherwise, just return the expression
   165	                    Ok(Transformed::no(child))
   166	                }
   167	            })
   168	            .data()
   169	        } else {
   170	            // If we don't have any remapped children, just return the expression
   171	            Ok(Arc::clone(&expr))
   172	        }
   173	    }
   174	
   175	    /// Get the current expression.
   176	    /// This will return the current expression with any children
   177	    /// remapped to match calls to [`PhysicalExpr::with_new_children`].
   178	    pub fn current(&self) -> Result<Arc<dyn PhysicalExpr>> {
   179	        let inner = Arc::clone(
   180	            &self
   181	                .inner
   182	                .read()
   183	                .map_err(|_| {
   184	                    datafusion_common::DataFusionError::Execution(
   185	                        "Failed to acquire read lock for inner".to_string(),
   186	                    )
   187	                })?
   188	                .expr,
   189	        );
   190	        let inner =
   191	            Self::remap_children(&self.children, self.remapped_children.as_ref(), inner)?;
   192	        Ok(inner)
   193	    }
   194	
   195	    /// Update the current expression.
   196	    /// Any children of this expression must be a subset of the original children
   197	    /// passed to the constructor.
   198	    /// This should be called e.g.:
   199	    /// - When we've computed the probe side's hash table in a HashJoinExec
   200	    /// - After every batch is processed if we update the TopK heap in a SortExec using a TopK approach.
   201	    pub fn update(&self, new_expr: Arc<dyn PhysicalExpr>) -> Result<()> {
   202	        let mut current = self.inner.write().map_err(|_| {
   203	            datafusion_common::DataFusionError::Execution(
   204	                "Failed to acquire write lock for inner".to_string(),
   205	            )
   206	        })?;
   207	        // Remap the children of the new expression to match the original children
   208	        // We still do this again in `current()` but doing it preventively here
   209	        // reduces the work needed in some cases if `current()` is called multiple times
   210	        // and the same externally facing `PhysicalExpr` is used for both `with_new_children` and `update()`.`
   211	        let new_expr = Self::remap_children(
   212	            &self.children,
   213	            self.remapped_children.as_ref(),
   214	            new_expr,
   215	        )?;
   216	        // Update the inner expression to the new expression.
   217	        current.expr = new_expr;
   218	        // Increment the generation to indicate that the expression has changed.
   219	        current.generation += 1;
   220	        Ok(())
   221	    }
   222	}
   223	
   224	impl PhysicalExpr for DynamicFilterPhysicalExpr {
   225	    fn as_any(&self) -> &dyn Any {
   226	        self
   227	    }
   228	
   229	    fn children(&self) -> Vec<&Arc<dyn PhysicalExpr>> {
   230	        self.remapped_children
   231	            .as_ref()
   232	            .unwrap_or(&self.children)
   233	            .iter()
   234	            .collect()
   235	    }
   236	
   237	    fn with_new_children(
   238	        self: Arc<Self>,
   239	        children: Vec<Arc<dyn PhysicalExpr>>,
   240	    ) -> Result<Arc<dyn PhysicalExpr>> {
   241	        Ok(Arc::new(Self {
   242	            children: self.children.clone(),
   243	            remapped_children: Some(children),
   244	            inner: Arc::clone(&self.inner),
   245	            data_type: Arc::clone(&self.data_type),
   246	            nullable: Arc::clone(&self.nullable),
   247	        }))
   248	    }
   249	
   250	    fn data_type(&self, input_schema: &Schema) -> Result<DataType> {
   251	        let res = self.current()?.data_type(input_schema)?;
   252	        #[cfg(test)]
   253	        {
   254	            use datafusion_common::internal_err;
   255	            // Check if the data type has changed.
   256	            let mut data_type_lock = self
   257	                .data_type
   258	                .write()
   259	                .expect("Failed to acquire write lock for data_type");
   260	            if let Some(existing) = &*data_type_lock {
   261	                if existing != &res {
   262	                    // If the data type has changed, we have a bug.
   263	                    return internal_err!(
   264	                        "DynamicFilterPhysicalExpr data type has changed unexpectedly. \
   265	                        Expected: {existing:?}, Actual: {res:?}"
   266	                    );
   267	                }
   268	            } else {
   269	                *data_type_lock = Some(res.clone());
   270	            }
   271	        }
   272	        Ok(res)
   273	    }
   274	
   275	    fn nullable(&self, input_schema: &Schema) -> Result<bool> {
   276	        let res = self.current()?.nullable(input_schema)?;
   277	        #[cfg(test)]
   278	        {
   279	            use datafusion_common::internal_err;
   280	            // Check if the nullability has changed.
   281	            let mut nullable_lock = self
   282	                .nullable
   283	                .write()
   284	                .expect("Failed to acquire write lock for nullable");
   285	            if let Some(existing) = *nullable_lock {
   286	                if existing != res {
   287	                    // If the nullability has changed, we have a bug.
   288	                    return internal_err!(
   289	                        "DynamicFilterPhysicalExpr nullability has changed unexpectedly. \
   290	                        Expected: {existing}, Actual: {res}"
   291	                    );
   292	                }
   293	            } else {
   294	                *nullable_lock = Some(res);
   295	            }
   296	        }
   297	        Ok(res)
   298	    }
   299	
   300	    fn evaluate(
   301	        &self,
   302	        batch: &arrow::record_batch::RecordBatch,
   303	    ) -> Result<ColumnarValue> {
   304	        let current = self.current()?;
   305	        #[cfg(test)]
   306	        {
   307	            // Ensure that we are not evaluating after the expression has changed.
   308	            let schema = batch.schema();
   309	            self.nullable(&schema)?;
   310	            self.data_type(&schema)?;
   311	        };
   312	        current.evaluate(batch)
   313	    }
   314	
   315	    fn fmt_sql(&self, f: &mut std::fmt::Formatter<'_>) -> std::fmt::Result {
   316	        let inner = self.current().map_err(|_| std::fmt::Error)?;
   317	        inner.fmt_sql(f)
   318	    }
   319	
   320	    fn snapshot(&self) -> Result<Option<Arc<dyn PhysicalExpr>>> {
   321	        // Return the current expression as a snapshot.
   322	        Ok(Some(self.current()?))
   323	    }
   324	
   325	    fn snapshot_generation(&self) -> u64 {
   326	        // Return the current generation of the expression.
   327	        self.inner
   328	            .read()
   329	            .expect("Failed to acquire read lock for inner")
   330	            .generation
   331	    }
   332	}

  1020	
  1021	    fn gather_filters_for_pushdown(
  1022	        &self,
  1023	        phase: FilterPushdownPhase,
  1024	        parent_filters: Vec<Arc<dyn PhysicalExpr>>,
  1025	        config: &ConfigOptions,
  1026	    ) -> Result<FilterDescription> {
  1027	        // Other types of joins can support *some* filters, but restrictions are complex and error prone.
  1028	        // For now we don't support them.
  1029	        // See the logical optimizer rules for more details: datafusion/optimizer/src/push_down_filter.rs
  1030	        // See https://github.com/apache/datafusion/issues/16973 for tracking.
  1031	        if self.join_type != JoinType::Inner {
  1032	            return Ok(FilterDescription::all_unsupported(
  1033	                &parent_filters,
  1034	                &self.children(),
  1035	            ));
  1036	        }
  1037	
  1038	        // Get basic filter descriptions for both children
  1039	        let left_child = crate::filter_pushdown::ChildFilterDescription::from_child(
  1040	            &parent_filters,
  1041	            self.left(),
  1042	        )?;
  1043	        let mut right_child = crate::filter_pushdown::ChildFilterDescription::from_child(
  1044	            &parent_filters,
  1045	            self.right(),
  1046	        )?;
  1047	
  1048	        // Add dynamic filters in Post phase if enabled
  1049	        if matches!(phase, FilterPushdownPhase::Post)
  1050	            && config.optimizer.enable_dynamic_filter_pushdown
  1051	        {
  1052	            // Add actual dynamic filter to right side (probe side)
  1053	            let dynamic_filter =
  1054	                Arc::clone(&self.dynamic_filter) as Arc<dyn PhysicalExpr>;
  1055	            right_child = right_child.with_self_filter(dynamic_filter);
  1056	        }
  1057	
  1058	        Ok(FilterDescription::new()
  1059	            .with_child(left_child)
  1060	            .with_child(right_child))
  1061	    }
  1062	
  1063	    fn handle_child_pushdown_result(
  1064	        &self,
  1065	        _phase: FilterPushdownPhase,
  1066	        child_pushdown_result: ChildPushdownResult,
  1067	        _config: &ConfigOptions,
  1068	    ) -> Result<FilterPushdownPropagation<Arc<dyn ExecutionPlan>>> {
  1069	        // Note: this check shouldn't be necessary because we already marked all parent filters as unsupported for
  1070	        // non-inner joins in `gather_filters_for_pushdown`.
  1071	        // However it's a cheap check and serves to inform future devs touching this function that they need to be really
  1072	        // careful pushing down filters through non-inner joins.
  1073	        if self.join_type != JoinType::Inner {
  1074	            // Other types of joins can support *some* filters, but restrictions are complex and error prone.
  1075	            // For now we don't support them.
  1076	            // See the logical optimizer rules for more details: datafusion/optimizer/src/push_down_filter.rs
  1077	            return Ok(FilterPushdownPropagation::all_unsupported(
  1078	                child_pushdown_result,
  1079	            ));
  1080	        }
  1081	        Ok(FilterPushdownPropagation::if_any(child_pushdown_result))
  1082	    }
  1083	}
  1084	
  1085	/// Compute min/max bounds for each column in the given arrays
  1086	fn compute_bounds(arrays: &[ArrayRef]) -> Result<Vec<(ScalarValue, ScalarValue)>> {
  1087	    arrays
  1088	        .iter()
  1089	        .map(|array| {
  1090	            if array.is_empty() {
  1091	                // Return NULL values for empty arrays
  1092	                return Ok((
  1093	                    ScalarValue::try_from(array.data_type())?,
  1094	                    ScalarValue::try_from(array.data_type())?,
  1095	                ));
  1096	            }
  1097	
  1098	            // Use Arrow kernels for efficient min/max computation
  1099	            let min_val = min_batch(array)?;
  1100	            let max_val = max_batch(array)?;
  1101	
  1102	            Ok((min_val, max_val))
  1103	        })
  1104	        .collect()
  1105	}

  1107	/// Reads the left (build) side of the input, buffering it in memory, to build a
  1108	/// hash table (`LeftJoinData`)
  1109	#[expect(clippy::too_many_arguments)]
  1110	async fn collect_left_input(
  1111	    random_state: RandomState,
  1112	    left_stream: SendableRecordBatchStream,
  1113	    on_left: Vec<PhysicalExprRef>,
  1114	    metrics: BuildProbeJoinMetrics,
  1115	    reservation: MemoryReservation,
  1116	    with_visited_indices_bitmap: bool,
  1117	    probe_threads_count: usize,
  1118	    dynamic_filter: Option<Arc<DynamicFilterPhysicalExpr>>,
  1119	    on_right: Vec<PhysicalExprRef>,
  1120	) -> Result<JoinLeftData> {
  1121	    let schema = left_stream.schema();
  1122	
  1123	    // This operation performs 2 steps at once:
  1124	    // 1. creates a [JoinHashMap] of all batches from the stream
  1125	    // 2. stores the batches in a vector.
  1126	    let initial = (Vec::new(), 0, metrics, reservation);
  1127	    let (batches, num_rows, metrics, mut reservation) = left_stream
  1128	        .try_fold(initial, |mut acc, batch| async {
  1129	            let batch_size = get_record_batch_memory_size(&batch);
  1130	            // Reserve memory for incoming batch
  1131	            acc.3.try_grow(batch_size)?;
  1132	            // Update metrics
  1133	            acc.2.build_mem_used.add(batch_size);
  1134	            acc.2.build_input_batches.add(1);
  1135	            acc.2.build_input_rows.add(batch.num_rows());
  1136	            // Update row count
  1137	            acc.1 += batch.num_rows();
  1138	            // Push batch to output
  1139	            acc.0.push(batch);
  1140	            Ok(acc)
  1141	        })
  1142	        .await?;
  1143	
  1144	    // Estimation of memory size, required for hashtable, prior to allocation.
  1145	    // Final result can be verified using `RawTable.allocation_info()`
  1146	    let fixed_size_u32 = size_of::<JoinHashMapU32>();
  1147	    let fixed_size_u64 = size_of::<JoinHashMapU64>();
  1148	
  1149	    // Use `u32` indices for the JoinHashMap when num_rows ≤ u32::MAX, otherwise use the
  1150	    // `u64` indice variant

   608	
   609	    /// Returns a new `ExecutionPlan` that computes the same join as this one,
   610	    /// with the left and right inputs swapped using the  specified
   611	    /// `partition_mode`.
   612	    ///
   613	    /// # Notes:
   614	    ///
   615	    /// This function is public so other downstream projects can use it to
   616	    /// construct `HashJoinExec` with right side as the build side.
   617	    pub fn swap_inputs(
   618	        &self,
   619	        partition_mode: PartitionMode,
   620	    ) -> Result<Arc<dyn ExecutionPlan>> {
   621	        let left = self.left();
   622	        let right = self.right();
   623	        let new_join = HashJoinExec::try_new(
   624	            Arc::clone(right),
   625	            Arc::clone(left),
   626	            self.on()
   627	                .iter()
   628	                .map(|(l, r)| (Arc::clone(r), Arc::clone(l)))
   629	                .collect(),
   630	            self.filter().map(JoinFilter::swap),
   631	            &self.join_type().swap(),
   632	            swap_join_projection(
   633	                left.schema().fields().len(),
   634	                right.schema().fields().len(),
   635	                self.projection.as_ref(),
   636	                self.join_type(),
   637	            ),
   638	            partition_mode,
   639	            self.null_equality(),
   640	        )?;
   641	        // In case of anti / semi joins or if there is embedded projection in HashJoinExec, output column order is preserved, no need to add projection again
   642	        if matches!(
   643	            self.join_type(),
   644	            JoinType::LeftSemi
   645	                | JoinType::RightSemi
   646	                | JoinType::LeftAnti
   647	                | JoinType::RightAnti
   648	        ) || self.projection.is_some()
   649	        {
   650	            Ok(Arc::new(new_join))
   651	        } else {
   652	            reorder_output_after_swap(Arc::new(new_join), &left.schema(), &right.schema())
   653	        }
   654	    }
   655	}

    18	//! The [`JoinSelection`] rule tries to modify a given plan so that it can
    19	//! accommodate infinite sources and utilize statistical information (if there
    20	//! is any) to obtain more performant plans. To achieve the first goal, it
    21	//! tries to transform a non-runnable query (with the given infinite sources)
    22	//! into a runnable query by replacing pipeline-breaking join operations with
    23	//! pipeline-friendly ones. To achieve the second goal, it selects the proper
    24	//! `PartitionMode` and the build side using the available statistics for hash joins.

    43	/// The [`JoinSelection`] rule tries to modify a given plan so that it can
    44	/// accommodate infinite sources and optimize joins in the plan according to
    45	/// available statistical information, if there is any.
    46	#[derive(Default, Debug)]
    47	pub struct JoinSelection {}
    48	
    49	impl JoinSelection {
    50	    #[allow(missing_docs)]
    51	    pub fn new() -> Self {
    52	        Self {}
    53	    }
    54	}
    55	
    56	// TODO: We need some performance test for Right Semi/Right Join swap to Left Semi/Left Join in case that the right side is smaller but not much smaller.
    57	// TODO: In PrestoSQL, the optimizer flips join sides only if one side is much smaller than the other by more than SIZE_DIFFERENCE_THRESHOLD times, by default is 8 times.
    58	/// Checks statistics for join swap.
    59	pub(crate) fn should_swap_join_order(
    60	    left: &dyn ExecutionPlan,
    61	    right: &dyn ExecutionPlan,
    62	) -> Result<bool> {
    63	    // Get the left and right table's total bytes
    64	    // If both the left and right tables contain total_byte_size statistics,
    65	    // use `total_byte_size` to determine `should_swap_join_order`, else use `num_rows`
    66	    let left_stats = left.partition_statistics(None)?;
    67	    let right_stats = right.partition_statistics(None)?;
    68	    // First compare `total_byte_size` of left and right side,
    69	    // if information in this field is insufficient fallback to the `num_rows`
    70	    match (
    71	        left_stats.total_byte_size.get_value(),
    72	        right_stats.total_byte_size.get_value(),
    73	    ) {
    74	        (Some(l), Some(r)) => Ok(l > r),
    75	        _ => match (
    76	            left_stats.num_rows.get_value(),
    77	            right_stats.num_rows.get_value(),
    78	        ) {
    79	            (Some(l), Some(r)) => Ok(l > r),
    80	            _ => Ok(false),
    81	        },
    82	    }
    83	}
    84	
    85	fn supports_collect_by_thresholds(
    86	    plan: &dyn ExecutionPlan,
    87	    threshold_byte_size: usize,
    88	    threshold_num_rows: usize,
    89	) -> bool {
    90	    // Currently we do not trust the 0 value from stats, due to stats collection might have bug
    91	    // TODO check the logic in datasource::get_statistics_with_limit()
    92	    let Ok(stats) = plan.partition_statistics(None) else {
    93	        return false;
    94	    };
    95	
    96	    if let Some(byte_size) = stats.total_byte_size.get_value() {
    97	        *byte_size != 0 && *byte_size < threshold_byte_size
    98	    } else if let Some(num_rows) = stats.num_rows.get_value() {
    99	        *num_rows != 0 && *num_rows < threshold_num_rows
   100	    } else {

   225	/// Creates a partitioned hash join execution plan, swapping inputs if beneficial.
   226	///
   227	/// Checks if the join order should be swapped based on the join type and input statistics.
   228	/// If swapping is optimal and supported, creates a swapped partitioned hash join; otherwise,
   229	/// creates a standard partitioned hash join.
   230	pub(crate) fn partitioned_hash_join(
   231	    hash_join: &HashJoinExec,
   232	) -> Result<Arc<dyn ExecutionPlan>> {
   233	    let left = hash_join.left();
   234	    let right = hash_join.right();
   235	    if hash_join.join_type().supports_swap() && should_swap_join_order(&**left, &**right)?
   236	    {
   237	        hash_join.swap_inputs(PartitionMode::Partitioned)

   372	impl HashJoinExec {
   373	    /// Tries to create a new [HashJoinExec].
   374	    ///
   375	    /// # Error
   376	    /// This function errors when it is not possible to join the left and right sides on keys `on`.
   377	    #[allow(clippy::too_many_arguments)]
   378	    pub fn try_new(
   379	        left: Arc<dyn ExecutionPlan>,
   380	        right: Arc<dyn ExecutionPlan>,
   381	        on: JoinOn,
   382	        filter: Option<JoinFilter>,
   383	        join_type: &JoinType,
   384	        projection: Option<Vec<usize>>,
   385	        partition_mode: PartitionMode,
   386	        null_equality: NullEquality,
   387	    ) -> Result<Self> {
   388	        let left_schema = left.schema();
   389	        let right_schema = right.schema();
   390	        if on.is_empty() {
   391	            return plan_err!("On constraints in HashJoinExec should be non-empty");
   392	        }

   396	        let (join_schema, column_indices) =

   398	
   399	        let random_state = HASH_JOIN_SEED;

   412	            partition_mode,
   413	            projection.as_ref(),
   414	        )?;
   415	
   416	        let dynamic_filter = Self::create_dynamic_filter(&on);
   417	
   418	        Ok(HashJoinExec {

   423	            join_type: *join_type,
   424	            join_schema,
   425	            left_fut: Default::default(),
   426	            random_state,
   427	            mode: partition_mode,
   428	            metrics: ExecutionPlanMetricsSet::new(),
   429	            projection,
   430	            column_indices,
   431	            null_equality,
   432	            cache,
   433	            dynamic_filter,
   434	        })
   435	    }
   436	
   437	    fn create_dynamic_filter(on: &JoinOn) -> Arc<DynamicFilterPhysicalExpr> {
   438	        // Extract the right-side keys from the `on` clauses
   439	        let right_keys: Vec<_> = on.iter().map(|(_, r)| Arc::clone(r)).collect();
   440	        // Initialize with a placeholder expression (true) that will be updated when the hash table is built
   441	        Arc::new(DynamicFilterPhysicalExpr::new(right_keys, lit(true)))
   442	    }
   443

   617	    pub fn swap_inputs(
   618	        &self,
   619	        partition_mode: PartitionMode,
   620	    ) -> Result<Arc<dyn ExecutionPlan>> {
   621	        let left = self.left();
   622	        let right = self.right();
   623	        let new_join = HashJoinExec::try_new(
   624	            Arc::clone(right),
   625	            Arc::clone(left),
   626	            self.on()
   627	                .iter()
   628	                .map(|(l, r)| (Arc::clone(r), Arc::clone(l)))
   629	                .collect(),
   630	            self.filter().map(JoinFilter::swap),
   631	            &self.join_type().swap(),
   632	            swap_join_projection(
   633	                left.schema().fields().len(),
   634	                right.schema().fields().len(),
   635	                self.projection.as_ref(),
   636	                self.join_type(),
   637	            ),
   638	            partition_mode,
   639	            self.null_equality(),
   640	        )?;
   641	        // In case of anti / semi joins or if there is embedded projection in HashJoinExec, output column order is preserved, no need to add projection again
   642	        if matches!(
   643	            self.join_type(),
   644	            JoinType::LeftSemi
   645	                | JoinType::RightSemi
   646	                | JoinType::LeftAnti
   647	                | JoinType::RightAnti
   648	        ) || self.projection.is_some()
   649	        {
   650	            Ok(Arc::new(new_join))
   651	        } else {
   652	            reorder_output_after_swap(Arc::new(new_join), &left.schema(), &right.schema())
   653	        }
   654	    }
   655	}

Perfect! I can see the issue now. When `swap_inputs` is called:

1. Line 623: A new `HashJoinExec::try_new` is called
2. Lines 624-625: The inputs are swapped - `right` becomes the new left (build side), and `left` becomes the new right (probe side)
3. Lines 626-629: The join keys are swapped - `(l, r)` becomes `(r, l)`
4. Inside `try_new` (line 416): A new dynamic filter is created by calling `create_dynamic_filter(&on)`
5. In `create_dynamic_filter` (line 439): It extracts the right-side keys from the `on` clauses

The problem is that after swapping, the `on` clauses are `(r, l)` (swapped), so when `create_dynamic_filter` extracts the "right-side keys" (second element of the tuple), it gets `l` which are the keys from the original LEFT side. But these should be pushed to the probe side, which is now the original RIGHT side!

Let me verify this understanding by looking at `gather_filters_for_pushdown`:

  1021	    fn gather_filters_for_pushdown(
  1022	        &self,
  1023	        phase: FilterPushdownPhase,
  1024	        parent_filters: Vec<Arc<dyn PhysicalExpr>>,
  1025	        config: &ConfigOptions,
  1026	    ) -> Result<FilterDescription> {
  1027	        // Other types of joins can support *some* filters, but restrictions are complex and error prone.
  1028	        // For now we don't support them.
  1029	        // See the logical optimizer rules for more details: datafusion/optimizer/src/push_down_filter.rs
  1030	        // See https://github.com/apache/datafusion/issues/16973 for tracking.
  1031	        if self.join_type != JoinType::Inner {
  1032	            return Ok(FilterDescription::all_unsupported(
  1033	                &parent_filters,
  1034	                &self.children(),
  1035	            ));
  1036	        }
  1037	
  1038	        // Get basic filter descriptions for both children
  1039	        let left_child = crate::filter_pushdown::ChildFilterDescription::from_child(
  1040	            &parent_filters,
  1041	            self.left(),
  1042	        )?;
  1043	        let mut right_child = crate::filter_pushdown::ChildFilterDescription::from_child(
  1044	            &parent_filters,
  1045	            self.right(),
  1046	        )?;
  1047	
  1048	        // Add dynamic filters in Post phase if enabled
  1049	        if matches!(phase, FilterPushdownPhase::Post)
  1050	            && config.optimizer.enable_dynamic_filter_pushdown
  1051	        {
  1052	            // Add actual dynamic filter to right side (probe side)
  1053	            let dynamic_filter =
  1054	                Arc::clone(&self.dynamic_filter) as Arc<dyn PhysicalExpr>;
  1055	            right_child = right_child.with_self_filter(dynamic_filter);
  1056	        }
  1057	
  1058	        Ok(FilterDescription::new()
  1059	            .with_child(left_child)
  1060	            .with_child(right_child))
  1061	    }

Ah! I see the issue. At line 1055, the dynamic filter is added to `right_child` unconditionally. The comment at line 1052 says "Add actual dynamic filter to right side (probe side)", which is correct in principle.

However, the problem is that the `dynamic_filter` field itself contains the wrong keys after a swap. Let me trace through what happens:

**Before swap:**
- Left side (build): t1 (1M rows) 
- Right side (probe): t2 (filtered to 1 row)
- `on` clauses: `[(t1.k, t2.k)]`
- `dynamic_filter` created with right keys: `[t2.k]` ✓ Correct - should be pushed to probe side

**After swap (when t2 has 9M rows):**
- Left side (build): t2 (1M rows from t1)  ← was originally right
- Right side (probe): t1 (1M rows) ← was originally left
- `on` clauses after swap: `[(t2.k, t1.k)]` ← note the swap
- `dynamic_filter` created with right keys: `[t1.k]` ✗ Wrong! These are columns from the original left side (which is now the right/probe side)

The dynamic filter should contain columns from the build side (left side after swap, which was originally the right side), not the probe side!

Now I understand. Let me create a test to reproduce the issue:

create external table t2 stored as parquet location '"'"'t2.parquet'"'"';

where t2.v = 1000000;

-- Test 2: Pushed to wrong relation (large right side, left becomes build side)
explain analyze select *
from t1
join t2 on t1.k = t2.k
where t2.v >= 1000000;
'

This test shows that the dynamic filter is expected to be pushed to the probe side (right side). Let me now think about what the fix should be.

The problem is clear:
1. When a `HashJoinExec` is created, the `dynamic_filter` is initialized with the right side keys (probe side keys)
2. When `swap_inputs` is called, the left and right sides are swapped, but the `dynamic_filter` is re-created with the new "right side" keys
3. However, after the swap, the new "right side" contains the original left side, so the dynamic filter now has the wrong keys

The fix should be: When we swap inputs, we need to ensure that the dynamic filter uses the keys from the new build side (new left), not the new probe side (new right).

Let me re-think this:

1. In a hash join, the left side is the build side (used to build the hash table), and the right side is the probe side (probed against the hash table)
2. The dynamic filter is created from the probe side keys (right side keys) 
3. The dynamic filter is pushed down to the probe side to filter rows before they reach the join

So when we swap:
- Original: left=build(t1), right=probe(t2), on=[(t1.k, t2.k)]
- After swap: left=build(t2), right=probe(t1), on=[(t2.k, t1.k)]
- Dynamic filter should use keys from the new probe side: t1.k ✓

The issue says:
> Now if the `t2` side is greater than `t1`, then the order of the join switches, as the smaller relation becomes the build side. However, the Dynamic Filter Pushdown is still applied to the right relation (now `t2`) instead of `t1`:

So the problem is:
- When t2 has 9M rows and t1 has 1M rows
- The optimizer decides to swap so t1 becomes the build side (left)
- After swap: left=t1 (build, 1M rows), right=t2 (probe, 9M rows)

Actually, wait. Let me re-read the expected behavior from the issue:

Looking at the first query (which works):
```
HashJoinExec join_type=Inner
    DataSourceExec t2.parquet (build side, 1 row)
        predicate=v@1 = 1000000
        output_rows=1
    DataSourceExec t1.parquet (probe side, 1M rows)
        predicate=DynamicFilterPhysicalExpr [ k@0 >= 1000000 AND k@0 <= 1000000 ]
        output_rows=1
```

So t2 is on the left (build side), t1 is on the right (probe side), and the dynamic filter is pushed to t1 (probe side) with a range based on t2.k values.

Looking at the second query (which doesn't work):
```
HashJoinExec join_type=Inner
    DataSourceExec t1.parquet (build side, 1M rows)
        output_rows=1000000
    DataSourceExec t2.parquet (probe side, 9M rows)
        predicate=v@1 >= 1000000 AND DynamicFilterPhysicalExpr [ k@0 >= 3 AND k@0 <= 999998 ]
        output_rows=0
```

So t1 is on the left (build side), t2 is on the right (probe side), and the dynamic filter is pushed to t2 (probe side). But the range `[ k@0 >= 3 AND k@0 <= 999998 ]` seems to be based on t1.k values (which range from 1 to 1M).

The issue is that the dynamic filter should be applied to the probe side to filter based on what's in the build side's hash table. So if t1 (1 to 1M) is the build side, the dynamic filter should filter t2 to only include rows where t2.k is in the range [1, 1M]. But t2 has values from 1 to 10M, so we should filter out rows where t2.k > 1M.

So the filter `k@0 >= 3 AND k@0 <= 999998` seems wrong - it should be `k@0 >= 1 AND k@0 <= 1000000`.

  1107	/// Reads the left (build) side of the input, buffering it in memory, to build a
  1108	/// hash table (`LeftJoinData`)
  1109	#[expect(clippy::too_many_arguments)]
  1110	async fn collect_left_input(
  1111	    random_state: RandomState,
  1112	    left_stream: SendableRecordBatchStream,
  1113	    on_left: Vec<PhysicalExprRef>,
  1114	    metrics: BuildProbeJoinMetrics,
  1115	    reservation: MemoryReservation,
  1116	    with_visited_indices_bitmap: bool,
  1117	    probe_threads_count: usize,
  1118	    dynamic_filter: Option<Arc<DynamicFilterPhysicalExpr>>,
  1119	    on_right: Vec<PhysicalExprRef>,
  1120	) -> Result<JoinLeftData> {
  1121	    let schema = left_stream.schema();
  1122	
  1123	    // This operation performs 2 steps at once:
  1124	    // 1. creates a [JoinHashMap] of all batches from the stream
  1125	    // 2. stores the batches in a vector.
  1126	    let initial = (Vec::new(), 0, metrics, reservation);
  1127	    let (batches, num_rows, metrics, mut reservation) = left_stream
  1128	        .try_fold(initial, |mut acc, batch| async {
  1129	            let batch_size = get_record_batch_memory_size(&batch);
  1130	            // Reserve memory for incoming batch
  1131	            acc.3.try_grow(batch_size)?;
  1132	            // Update metrics
  1133	            acc.2.build_mem_used.add(batch_size);
  1134	            acc.2.build_input_batches.add(1);
  1135	            acc.2.build_input_rows.add(batch.num_rows());
  1136	            // Update row count
  1137	            acc.1 += batch.num_rows();
  1138	            // Push batch to output
  1139	            acc.0.push(batch);
  1140	            Ok(acc)
  1141	        })
  1142	        .await?;
  1143	
  1144	    // Estimation of memory size, required for hashtable, prior to allocation.
  1145	    // Final result can be verified using `RawTable.allocation_info()`
  1146	    let fixed_size_u32 = size_of::<JoinHashMapU32>();
  1147	    let fixed_size_u64 = size_of::<JoinHashMapU64>();
  1148	
  1149	    // Use `u32` indices for the JoinHashMap when num_rows ≤ u32::MAX, otherwise use the
  1150	    // `u64` indice variant
  1151	    let mut hashmap: Box<dyn JoinHashMapType> = if num_rows > u32::MAX as usize {
  1152	        let estimated_hashtable_size =
  1153	            estimate_memory_size::<(u64, u64)>(num_rows, fixed_size_u64)?;
  1154	        reservation.try_grow(estimated_hashtable_size)?;
  1155	        metrics.build_mem_used.add(estimated_hashtable_size);
  1156	        Box::new(JoinHashMapU64::with_capacity(num_rows))
  1157	    } else {
  1158	        let estimated_hashtable_size =
  1159	            estimate_memory_size::<(u32, u64)>(num_rows, fixed_size_u32)?;
  1160	        reservation.try_grow(estimated_hashtable_size)?;
  1161	        metrics.build_mem_used.add(estimated_hashtable_size);
  1162	        Box::new(JoinHashMapU32::with_capacity(num_rows))
  1163	    };
  1164	
  1165	    let mut hashes_buffer = Vec::new();
  1166	    let mut offset = 0;
  1167	
  1168	    // Updating hashmap starting from the last batch
  1169	    let batches_iter = batches.iter().rev();
  1170	    for batch in batches_iter.clone() {
  1171	        hashes_buffer.clear();
  1172	        hashes_buffer.resize(batch.num_rows(), 0);
  1173	        update_hash(
  1174	            &on_left,
  1175	            batch,
  1176	            &mut *hashmap,
  1177	            offset,
  1178	            &random_state,
  1179	            &mut hashes_buffer,
  1180	            0,
  1181	            true,
  1182	        )?;
  1183	        offset += batch.num_rows();
  1184	    }
  1185	    // Merge all batches into a single batch, so we can directly index into the arrays
  1186	    let single_batch = concat_batches(&schema, batches_iter)?;
  1187	
  1188	    // Reserve additional memory for visited indices bitmap and create shared builder
  1189	    let visited_indices_bitmap = if with_visited_indices_bitmap {
  1190	        let bitmap_size = bit_util::ceil(single_batch.num_rows(), 8);
  1191	        reservation.try_grow(bitmap_size)?;
  1192	        metrics.build_mem_used.add(bitmap_size);
  1193	
  1194	        let mut bitmap_buffer = BooleanBufferBuilder::new(single_batch.num_rows());
  1195	        bitmap_buffer.append_n(num_rows, false);
  1196	        bitmap_buffer
  1197	    } else {
  1198	        BooleanBufferBuilder::new(0)
  1199	    };
  1200	
  1201	    let left_values = on_left
  1202	        .iter()
  1203	        .map(|c| {
  1204	            c.evaluate(&single_batch)?
  1205	                .into_array(single_batch.num_rows())
  1206	        })
  1207	        .collect::<Result<Vec<_>>>()?;
  1208	
  1209	    let data = JoinLeftData::new(
  1210	        hashmap,
  1211	        single_batch,
  1212	        left_values.clone(),
  1213	        Mutex::new(visited_indices_bitmap),
  1214	        AtomicUsize::new(probe_threads_count),
  1215	        reservation,
  1216	    );
  1217	
  1218	    // Update dynamic filter with min/max bounds if provided
  1219	    if let Some(dynamic_filter) = dynamic_filter {
  1220	        if num_rows > 0 {
  1221	            let bounds = compute_bounds(&left_values)?;
  1222	
  1223	            // Create range predicates for each join key
  1224	            let mut predicates = Vec::with_capacity(bounds.len());
  1225	            for ((min_val, max_val), right_expr) in bounds.iter().zip(on_right.iter()) {
  1226	                // Create predicate: col >= min AND col <= max
  1227	                let min_expr = Arc::new(BinaryExpr::new(
  1228	                    Arc::clone(right_expr),
  1229	                    Operator::GtEq,
  1230	                    lit(min_val.clone()),
  1231	                )) as Arc<dyn PhysicalExpr>;
  1232	
  1233	                let max_expr = Arc::new(BinaryExpr::new(
  1234	                    Arc::clone(right_expr),
  1235	                    Operator::LtEq,
  1236	                    lit(max_val.clone()),
  1237	                )) as Arc<dyn PhysicalExpr>;
  1238	
  1239	                let range_expr =
  1240	                    Arc::new(BinaryExpr::new(min_expr, Operator::And, max_expr))
  1241	                        as Arc<dyn PhysicalExpr>;
  1242	
  1243	                predicates.push(range_expr);
  1244	            }
  1245	
  1246	            // Combine all predicates with AND
  1247	            let combined_predicate = predicates
  1248	                .into_iter()
  1249	                .reduce(|acc, pred| {
  1250	                    Arc::new(BinaryExpr::new(acc, Operator::And, pred))
  1251	                        as Arc<dyn PhysicalExpr>
  1252	                })
  1253	                .unwrap_or_else(|| lit(true));
  1254	
  1255	            dynamic_filter.update(combined_predicate)?;
  1256	        }
  1257	    }
  1258	
  1259	    Ok(data)
  1260	}
  1261	
  1262	/// Updates `hash_map` with new entries from `batch` evaluated against the expressions `on`
  1263	/// using `offset` as a start value for `batch` row indices.
  1264	///
  1265	/// `fifo_hashmap` sets the order of iteration over `batch` rows while updating hashmap,
  1266	/// which allows to keep either first (if set to true) or last (if set to false) row index
  1267	/// as a chain head for rows with equal hash values.
  1268	#[allow(clippy::too_many_arguments)]
  1269	pub fn update_hash(
  1270	    on: &[PhysicalExprRef],
  1271	    batch: &RecordBatch,
  1272	    hash_map: &mut dyn JoinHashMapType,
  1273	    offset: usize,
  1274	    random_state: &RandomState,
  1275	    hashes_buffer: &mut Vec<u64>,
  1276	    deleted_offset: usize,
  1277	    fifo_hashmap: bool,
  1278	) -> Result<()> {
  1279	    // evaluate the keys
  1280	    let keys_values = on

```

The `on_right` are the expressions from the right side (probe side) of the join. The bounds are computed from `left_values` (build side). So the filter says: "right_expr >= min_value_from_left".

Now let me trace what happens with `swap_inputs`:

1. Original join: `left=t1, right=t2, on=[(t1.k, t2.k)]`
   - `on_left = [t1.k]`, `on_right = [t2.k]`
   - Dynamic filter created with: `right_keys = [t2.k]` (from `create_dynamic_filter`)
   - When building, uses: `on_left = [t1.k]` (to compute bounds), `on_right = [t2.k]` (to create predicates)
   - Result: filter is `t2.k >= min(t1.k) AND t2.k <= max(t1.k)` ✓

2. After swap: `left=t2, right=t1, on=[(t2.k, t1.k)]`
   - `on_left = [t2.k]`, `on_right = [t1.k]`
   - Dynamic filter created with: `right_keys = [t1.k]` (from `create_dynamic_filter`)
   - When building, uses: `on_left = [t2.k]` (to compute bounds), `on_right = [t1.k]` (to create predicates)
   - Result: filter is `t1.k >= min(t2.k) AND t1.k <= max(t2.k)` ✓

Wait, that seems correct! The dynamic filter uses the probe side keys (`on_right`), and when building the filter, it computes bounds from the build side (`on_left`) and creates predicates using the probe side keys (`on_right`).

  1086	fn compute_bounds(arrays: &[ArrayRef]) -> Result<Vec<(ScalarValue, ScalarValue)>> {
  1087	    arrays
  1088	        .iter()
  1089	        .map(|array| {
  1090	            if array.is_empty() {
  1091	                // Return NULL values for empty arrays
  1092	                return Ok((
  1093	                    ScalarValue::try_from(array.data_type())?,
  1094	                    ScalarValue::try_from(array.data_type())?,
  1095	                ));
  1096	            }
  1097	
  1098	            // Use Arrow kernels for efficient min/max computation
  1099	            let min_val = min_batch(array)?;
  1100	            let max_val = max_batch(array)?;
  1101	
  1102	            Ok((min_val, max_val))

- Build side: Smaller table, used to build a hash table
- Probe side: Larger table, probed against the hash table

The dynamic filter is meant to reduce the amount of data scanned from the probe side by pushing down a filter based on what's in the build side's hash table.

In Query 1:
- t2 (1 row) is build side
- t1 (1M rows) is probe side

- t2 (9M rows) is probe side

    18	//! Physical column reference: [`Column`]
    19	
    20	use std::any::Any;
    21	use std::hash::Hash;
    22	use std::sync::Arc;
    23	
    24	use crate::physical_expr::PhysicalExpr;
    25	use arrow::datatypes::FieldRef;
    26	use arrow::{
    27	    datatypes::{DataType, Schema, SchemaRef},
    28	    record_batch::RecordBatch,
    29	};
    30	use datafusion_common::tree_node::{Transformed, TreeNode};
    31	use datafusion_common::{internal_err, plan_err, Result};
    32	use datafusion_expr::ColumnarValue;
    33	
    34	/// Represents the column at a given index in a RecordBatch
    35	///
    36	/// This is a physical expression that represents a column at a given index in an
    37	/// arrow [`Schema`] / [`RecordBatch`].
    38	///
    39	/// Unlike the [logical `Expr::Column`], this expression is always resolved by schema index,
    40	/// even though it does have a name. This is because the physical plan is always
    41	/// resolved to a specific schema and there is no concept of "relation"
    42	///
    43	/// # Example:
    44	///  If the schema is `a`, `b`, `c` the `Column` for `b` would be represented by
    45	///  index 1, since `b` is the second column in the schema.
    46	///
    47	/// ```
    48	/// # use datafusion_physical_expr::expressions::Column;
    49	/// # use arrow::datatypes::{DataType, Field, Schema};
    50	/// // Schema with columns a, b, c
    51	/// let schema = Schema::new(vec![
    52	///    Field::new("a", DataType::Int32, false),
    53	///    Field::new("b", DataType::Int32, false),
    54	///    Field::new("c", DataType::Int32, false),
    55	/// ]);
    56	///
    57	/// // reference to column b is index 1
    58	/// let column_b = Column::new_with_schema("b", &schema).unwrap();
    59	/// assert_eq!(column_b.index(), 1);
    60	///
    61	/// // reference to column c is index 2
    62	/// let column_c = Column::new_with_schema("c", &schema).unwrap();
    63	/// assert_eq!(column_c.index(), 2);
    64	/// ```
    65	/// [logical `Expr::Column`]: https://docs.rs/datafusion/latest/datafusion/logical_expr/enum.Expr.html#variant.Column
    66	#[derive(Debug, Hash, PartialEq, Eq, Clone)]
    67	pub struct Column {
    68	    /// The name of the column (used for debugging and display purposes)
    69	    name: String,
    70	    /// The index of the column in its schema
    71	    index: usize,
    72	}
    73	
    74	impl Column {
    75	    /// Create a new column expression which references the
    76	    /// column with the given index in the schema.
    77	    pub fn new(name: &str, index: usize) -> Self {
    78	        Self {
    79	            name: name.to_owned(),
    80	            index,
    81	        }
    82	    }
    83	
    84	    /// Create a new column expression which references the
    85	    /// column with the given name in the schema
    86	    pub fn new_with_schema(name: &str, schema: &Schema) -> Result<Self> {
    87	        Ok(Column::new(name, schema.index_of(name)?))
    88	    }
    89	
    90	    /// Get the column's name
    91	    pub fn name(&self) -> &str {
    92	        &self.name
    93	    }
    94	
    95	    /// Get the column's schema index
    96	    pub fn index(&self) -> usize {
    97	        self.index
    98	    }
    99	}
   100

Perfect! So `Column` has both a name and an index. The index is what's used to reference the actual column in a `RecordBatch`.

Now, when we swap the join inputs, the column expressions in the join keys are swapped at lines 626-629:

```rust
self.on()
    .iter()
    .map(|(l, r)| (Arc::clone(r), Arc::clone(l)))
    .collect()
```

But these column expressions still have their original indices! For example:
- Original: `t1.k` has index 0 in t1's schema, `t2.k` has index 0 in t2's schema
- After swap: The new `on` clauses are `[(t2.k, t1.k)]`, but:
  - `t2.k` still has index 0 in the ORIGINAL t2 schema
  - `t1.k` still has index 0 in the ORIGINAL t1 schema

So when the dynamic filter is created with `right_keys = [t1.k]`, and this filter is pushed to the right child (which is now t1), the column reference should still be correct because `t1.k` has index 0 in t1's schema!

Hmm, so that's not the issue either...

Wait, let me re-read the logic in `gather_filters_for_pushdown` one more time. The key line is:

```rust
right_child = right_child.with_self_filter(dynamic_filter);
```

This adds the dynamic filter to the right child. The dynamic filter contains column references for the probe side (right side). So far so good.

But wait! Let me check what happens in `collect_left_input`. The dynamic filter is created with `right_keys`, which are the probe side keys. Then in `collect_left_input`, at lines 1225-1243, it creates predicates like:

```rust
for ((min_val, max_val), right_expr) in bounds.iter().zip(on_right.iter()) {
    let min_expr = Arc::new(BinaryExpr::new(
        Arc::clone(right_expr),
        Operator::GtEq,
        lit(min_val.clone()),
    )) as Arc<dyn PhysicalExpr>;
    ...
}
```

So it uses `on_right` to create the predicates! And `on_right` is passed as a parameter to `collect_left_input`.

Let me check what's passed as `on_right` at lines 890 and 910:

```rust
on_right.clone(),
```

And `on_right` is defined at lines 843-847:

```rust
let on_right = self
    .on
    .iter()
    .map(|on| Arc::clone(&on.1))
    .collect::<Vec<_>>();
```

So `on_right` is extracted from `self.on` (the right side of each tuple). And `self.on` was set when the `HashJoinExec` was created.

Ahh! I think I see the issue now! Let me trace through it one more time:

**After swap:**
1. `swap_inputs` calls `HashJoinExec::try_new` with:
   - `left = original_right`
   - `right = original_left`
   - `on = [(original_r, original_l)]` (swapped)
2. In `try_new`, `create_dynamic_filter(&on)` is called
3. `create_dynamic_filter` extracts right keys: `[original_l]`
4. The dynamic filter is created with children `[original_l]`
5. Later, in `execute`, `on_right` is extracted from `self.on`: `[original_l]`
6. In `collect_left_input`, predicates are created using `on_right`: `[original_l]`
7. The filter is: `original_l >= min(original_r) AND original_l <= max(original_r)`
8. The filter is pushed to the right child, which is `original_left`

So the filter says: "`original_left` columns should be in the range of `original_right` values", and it's pushed to the `original_left` table.

But this is correct! If `original_right` is the build side (smaller table), then we want to filter `original_left` (the probe side) to only include rows that could potentially match the build side.

Wait, I'm getting confused again. Let me create a concrete example:

**Scenario:**
- t1 has 1M rows with k values [1, 1000000]
- t2 has 9M rows with k values [1, 10000000], but filtered to rows where v >= 1000000, which gives 9M rows
- The optimizer decides t1 (1M rows) should be the build side

**Expected behavior after swap:**
- Build side (left): t1 with k values [1, 1000000]
- Probe side (right): t2 with k values [1, 10000000]
- Dynamic filter should filter t2 to only rows where t2.k is in [1, 1000000]
- This reduces t2 from 9M rows to 1M rows

**What actually happens (based on the code):**
- `on = [(t1.k, t2.k)]`
- Dynamic filter created with right keys: `[t2.k]`
- In `collect_left_input`:
  - `on_left = [t1.k]`
  - `on_right = [t2.k]`
  - Bounds computed from t1.k values: [1, 1000000]
  - Predicates created: `t2.k >= 1 AND t2.k <= 1000000`
- Filter pushed to right child: t2
- Result: t2 is filtered to [1, 1000000] ✓ Correct!

So based on my analysis, the code should be working correctly! Let me look at the issue description one more time to see if I'm misunderstanding something...

Oh! I just realized something. The issue description says:

> The Dynamic Filter Pushdown is still applied to the right relation (now `t2`) instead of `t1`

I think the issue reporter is confused about which table should get the filter. Let me re-read the two query outputs:

**Query 1:**
```
HashJoinExec
    DataSourceExec t2.parquet (1 row)
    DataSourceExec t1.parquet (1M rows)
        predicate=DynamicFilterPhysicalExpr [ k@0 >= 1000000 AND k@0 <= 1000000 ]
```

**Query 2:**
```
HashJoinExec
    DataSourceExec t1.parquet (1M rows)
    DataSourceExec t2.parquet (9M rows)
        predicate=v@1 >= 1000000 AND DynamicFilterPhysicalExpr [ k@0 >= 3 AND k@0 <= 999998 ]
```

Ahh! Now I see the real issue! In Query 2, the dynamic filter is on t2, but t2 is the LARGER table (9M rows). The dynamic filter should be pushed to the table that needs to be filtered down to match the build side, which in this case is t2, so that's correct.

But wait, the issue says the filter results in "output_rows=0" for t2. That doesn't make sense if the filter is `k@0 >= 3 AND k@0 <= 999998` and t2 has values from 1 to 10M.

> However, the Dynamic Filter Pushdown is still applied to the right relation (now `t2`) instead of `t1`

I think the reporter is saying that the dynamic filter SHOULD be applied to t1, not t2. But why?

Ohhhh! I think I finally get it! The reporter might be thinking that since t1 is the build side (left), it should get the dynamic filter. But that doesn't make sense because you can't filter the build side based on the probe side's values - you build the hash table first, then probe it!

Unless... maybe the reporter is thinking about a different optimization where you filter both sides based on join key predicates? Like if there's a predicate `t2.v >= 1000000`, maybe we could infer that `t1.k` only needs to include values that exist in the filtered t2?
